1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_ref-13)**Defining the rotation as retrograde, as done by NASA space missions and the USGS, puts [Ishtar Terra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ishtar_Terra "Ishtar Terra") in the northern hemisphere and makes the axial tilt 2.64°. Following the [right-hand rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-hand_rule "Right-hand rule") for prograde rotation puts Ishtar Terra in the negative hemisphere and makes the axial tilt 177.36°.

**Venus** is the second [planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planet "Planet") from the [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun"). It is often called [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth")'s "twin" or "sister" among the planets of the [Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System "Solar System") for its orbit being the closest to Earth's, both being [rocky planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocky_planet "Rocky planet") and having the most similar and nearly equal size and mass. Venus, though, differs significantly by having no [liquid water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid_water "Liquid water"), and [its atmosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus "Atmosphere of Venus") is far thicker and denser than that of any other rocky body in the Solar System. It is composed of mostly [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide") and has a cloud layer of [sulfuric acid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulfuric_acid "Sulfuric acid") that spans the whole planet. At the mean surface level, the atmosphere reaches a temperature of 737 K (464°C; 867°F) and a [pressure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure "Atmospheric pressure") 92 times greater than Earth's at sea level, turning the lowest layer of the atmosphere into a [supercritical fluid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercritical_fluid "Supercritical fluid"). From Earth Venus is visible as a star-like point of light, [appearing brighter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_brightness "Apparent brightness") than any other natural point of light in Earth's sky,[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lawrence_2005-22)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Walker_2017-23) and as an [inferior planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_planet "Inferior planet") always relatively close to the Sun, either as the brightest "morning star" or "evening star”.

The orbits of Venus and Earth make the two planets approach each other in [synodic periods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synodic_period "Synodic period") of 1.6 years. In the course of this, Venus comes closer to Earth than any other planet, while on average [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)") stays closer to Earth and any other planet, due to its orbit being closer to the Sun. For [interplanetary spaceflights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_spaceflight "Interplanetary spaceflight"), Venus is frequently used as a waypoint for [gravity assists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist") because it offers a faster and more economical route. Venus has no [moons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moons "Moons") and a very slow [retrograde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrograde_and_prograde_motion "Retrograde and prograde motion") rotation about its axis, a result of competing forces of solar tidal locking and differential heating of Venus's massive atmosphere. As a result a Venusian day is 116.75 Earth days long, about half a Venusian [solar year](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_year "Solar year"), which is 224.7 Earth days long.

Venus has a weak [magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere "Magnetosphere"); lacking an [internal dynamo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamo_theory "Dynamo theory"), it is induced by the [solar wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind") interacting with the atmosphere. Internally, Venus has a [core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_core "Planetary core"),[mantle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantle_(geology) "Mantle (geology)"), and[crust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crust_(geology) "Crust (geology)"). [Internal heat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_heat "Internal heat") escapes through active [volcanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanism "Volcanism"),[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NYT-20240527-24)[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NA-20240527-25) resulting in [resurfacing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geology_of_Venus#Global_resurfacing_event "Geology of Venus"), instead of [plate tectonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics "Plate tectonics"). Venus may have had liquid surface water early in its history with a [habitable environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability"),[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NYT-20231026-26)[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NA-20231026-27) before a [runaway greenhouse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Runaway_greenhouse_effect "Runaway greenhouse effect") evaporated any water and turned Venus into its present state.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Jakosky-28)[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hashimoto_et_al_2008-29)[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Shiga_2007-30) Conditions at the cloud layer of Venus have been identified as possibly favourable for [life on Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_on_Venus "Life on Venus"), with potential biomarkers found in 2020, spurring new research and missions to Venus.

Humans have observed Venus throughout history across the globe, and it has acquired particular importance in many cultures. With telescopes, the [phases of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phases_of_Venus "Phases of Venus") became discernible and, by 1613, were presented as decisive evidence disproving the then-dominant [geocentric model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocentric_model "Geocentric model") and supporting the [heliocentric model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliocentric_model "Heliocentric model"). Venus was visited for the first time in 1961 by [Venera 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_1 "Venera 1"), which flew past the planet, achieving the first interplanetary spaceflight. The first data from Venus were returned during the second interplanetary mission, [Mariner 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_2 "Mariner 2"), in 1962. In 1967, the first interplanetary impactor, [Venera 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_4 "Venera 4"), reached Venus, followed by the lander [Venera 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_7 "Venera 7") in 1970. The data from these missions revealed the strong [greenhouse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_effect "Greenhouse effect") of carbon dioxide in its atmosphere, which raised concerns about increasing carbon dioxide levels in Earth's atmosphere and their role in driving [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change").[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Newitz_2013-31) As of 2025, [JUICE](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/JUICE "JUICE") and [Solar Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_Orbiter "Solar Orbiter") are on their way to fly-by Venus in 2025 and 2026 respectively, and the next mission planned to launch to Venus is the [Venus Life Finder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_Life_Finder "Venus Life Finder") scheduled for 2026.

Physical characteristics
------------------------

[![Image 3](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Terrestrial_planet_size_comp_2024.png/330px-Terrestrial_planet_size_comp_2024.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Terrestrial_planet_size_comp_2024.png)

Venus (second from the left, in false-colour) to scale among the [Inner Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inner_Solar_System "Inner Solar System")[planetary-mass objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary-mass_object "Planetary-mass object"), arranged by the order of their orbits outward from the Sun (from left: [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)"), Venus, [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth"), the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon"), [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars") and [Ceres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet) "Ceres (dwarf planet)"))

[![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/11214_2023_956_Fig3_HTML.webp/330px-11214_2023_956_Fig3_HTML.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:11214_2023_956_Fig3_HTML.webp)

Venus imaged in different wavelengths

Venus is one of the four [terrestrial planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrestrial_planet "Terrestrial planet") in the Solar System, meaning that it is a rocky body like Earth. It is similar to Earth in size and mass and is often described as Earth's "sister" or "twin".[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lopes_Gregg_2004-32) Venus is very close to spherical due to its slow rotation.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Venus-33) It has a diameter of 12,103.6 km (7,520.8 mi)—only 638.4 km (396.7 mi) less than Earth's—and its mass is 81.5% of Earth's, making it the third-smallest planet in the [Solar System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_System "Solar System"). Conditions on the surface of Venus differ radically from those on Earth because its dense [atmosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere "Atmosphere") is 96.5% carbon dioxide, causing an intense [greenhouse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_effect "Greenhouse effect"), with most of the remaining 3.5% being [nitrogen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nitrogen "Nitrogen").[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Darling_Venus-34) The surface pressure is 9.3 [megapascals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pascal_(unit) "Pascal (unit)") (93 [bars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_(unit) "Bar (unit)")), and the average surface temperature is 737 K (464°C; 867°F), above the [critical points](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critical_point_(thermodynamics) "Critical point (thermodynamics)") of both major constituents and making the surface atmosphere a [supercritical fluid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercritical_fluid "Supercritical fluid") of mainly [supercritical carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercritical_carbon_dioxide "Supercritical carbon dioxide") and some supercritical nitrogen.

### Formation

The rocky terrestrial planets including Venus are thought to have formed in 5 stages: dust settling, [planetesimal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetesimal "Planetesimal") formation, planetary embryos, giant impacts, and finally formation of atmospheres. Limited measurements from Venus have prevented a more detailed analysis of the formation timeline.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-35)

### Geography

[![Image 5](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/2438_pioneer_venus_map_of_venus.jpg/500px-2438_pioneer_venus_map_of_venus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2438_pioneer_venus_map_of_venus.jpg)

Colour-coded elevation map, showing the elevated [terrae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_nomenclature#Terra "Planetary nomenclature") "continents" in yellow and minor [features of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surface_features_of_Venus "Surface features of Venus")

[![Image 6](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Venus_globe.jpg/250px-Venus_globe.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_globe.jpg)

[Spherical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere "Sphere") view of radar data of the [surface of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mapping_of_Venus "Mapping of Venus"), highlighting [surface features](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_geological_features_on_Venus "List of geological features on Venus") (1989, [Magellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)")). The colours do not represent the appearance of the surface.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-k285-36)

The Venusian surface was a subject of speculation until some of its secrets were revealed by probes in the 20th century. _[Venera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera "Venera")_ landers in 1975 and 1982 returned images of a surface covered in sediment and relatively angular rocks.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mueller_2014-37) The surface was mapped in detail by [_Magellan_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)") in 1990–91. There is evidence of extensive volcanism, and variations in the atmospheric [sulphur dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulphur_dioxide "Sulphur dioxide") may indicate that there are active volcanoes.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Esposito_1984-38)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Bullock_Grinspoon_2001-39)

About 80% of the Venusian surface is covered by smooth, volcanic plains, consisting of 70% plains with wrinkle ridges and 10% smooth or lobate plains.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Basilevsky_Head_1995-40) Two [highland "continents"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Highland_continent "Highland continent") make up the rest of its surface area, one lying in the planet's northern hemisphere and the other just south of the equator. The northern continent is called [Ishtar Terra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ishtar_Terra "Ishtar Terra") after [Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ishtar "Ishtar"), the [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylon "Babylon") goddess of love, and is about the size of Australia. The [Maxwell Montes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell_Montes "Maxwell Montes") mountain range lies on Ishtar Terra. Its peak is the highest point on Venus, 11 km (7 mi) above the Venusian average surface elevation.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-planetology-41) The southern continent is called [Aphrodite Terra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphrodite_Terra "Aphrodite Terra"), after the [Greek mythological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_mythological "Greek mythological") goddess of love, and is the larger of the two highland regions at roughly the size of South America. A network of fractures and faults covers much of this area.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kaufmann-42)

There is recent evidence of [lava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lava "Lava") flow on Venus (2024),[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-43) such as flows on [Sif Mons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sif_Mons "Sif Mons"), a shield volcano, and on [Niobe Planitia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niobe_Planitia "Niobe Planitia"), a flat plain.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NYT-20240527-24) There are visible [calderas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caldera "Caldera"). The planet has few [impact craters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_crater "Impact crater"), demonstrating that the surface is relatively young, at 300–600 million years old.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nimmo98-44)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Strom1994-45) Venus has some unique surface features in addition to the impact craters, mountains, and valleys commonly found on rocky planets. Among these are flat-topped volcanic features called "[farra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farra_(Venus) "Farra (Venus)")", which look somewhat like pancakes and range in size from 20 to 50 km (12 to 31 mi) across, and from 100 to 1,000 m (330 to 3,280 ft) high; radial, star-like fracture systems called "novae"; features with both radial and concentric fractures resembling spider webs, known as "[arachnoids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arachnoid_(astrogeology) "Arachnoid (astrogeology)")"; and "coronae", circular rings of fractures sometimes surrounded by a depression. These features are volcanic in origin.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Frankel-46)

[![Image 7](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/USSR_Venera_9_1975_Venus_ground_colorized_by_Don_P._Mitchell.png/250px-USSR_Venera_9_1975_Venus_ground_colorized_by_Don_P._Mitchell.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:USSR_Venera_9_1975_Venus_ground_colorized_by_Don_P._Mitchell.png)

Colourized image ([Venera 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera_9 "Venera 9"), 1975), the colour of the Venusian sky is at the surface orange-yellow due to [rayleigh scattering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rayleigh_scattering "Rayleigh scattering") or a blue absorber in the lower atmosphere, being white at higher altitudes,[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-47)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-t069-48) while the surface it self is rather a [basalt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basalt "Basalt")-like dark gray, which is possibly oxidized red.[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-k285-36)

Most [Venusian surface features](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_geological_features_on_Venus "List of geological features on Venus") are named after historical and mythological women.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Batson_Russell_1991-49) Exceptions are Maxwell Montes, named after [James Clerk Maxwell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell "James Clerk Maxwell"), and highland regions [Alpha Regio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpha_Regio "Alpha Regio"), [Beta Regio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beta_Regio "Beta Regio"), and [Ovda Regio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovda_Regio "Ovda Regio"). The last three features were named before the current system was adopted by the [International Astronomical Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Astronomical_Union "International Astronomical Union"), the body which oversees [planetary nomenclature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_nomenclature "Planetary nomenclature").[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-jpl-magellan-50)

The longitude of physical features on Venus is expressed relative to its [prime meridian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_meridian "Prime meridian"). The original prime meridian passed through the radar-bright spot at the centre of the oval feature Eve, located south of Alpha Regio.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Davies_1994-51) After the Venera missions were completed, the prime meridian was redefined to pass through the central peak in the crater [Ariadne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariadne_(crater) "Ariadne (crater)") on [Sedna Planitia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedna_Planitia "Sedna Planitia").[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Seidelmann2007-8)[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-jpl-magellan2-52)

The stratigraphically oldest [tessera terrains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tessera_(Venus) "Tessera (Venus)") have consistently lower thermal emissivity than the surrounding basaltic plains measured by _[Venus Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus\_Express "Venus Express")_ and [_Magellan_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)"), indicating a different, possibly a more [felsic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felsic "Felsic"), mineral assemblage.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hashimoto_et_al_2008-29)[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Helbert_et_al_2008-53) The mechanism to generate a large amount of felsic crust usually requires the presence of a water ocean and [plate tectonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics "Plate tectonics"), implying that habitable condition existed on early Venus, with large bodies of water at some point.[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Petkowski_Seager_2021-54) However, the nature of tessera terrains is far from certain.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Gilmore_et_al_2017-55)

Studies reported in 2023 suggested for the first time that Venus may have had [plate tectonics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics "Plate tectonics") during ancient times and, as a result, may have had a more [habitable environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability"), possibly one capable of sustaining [life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_forms "Life forms").[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NYT-20231026-26)[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NA-20231026-27) Venus has gained interest as a case for research into the development of [Earth-like planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_analogue "Earth analogue") and [their habitability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability").

#### Volcanism

[![Image 8](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/PIA00084_Eistla_region_pancake_volcanoes.jpg/330px-PIA00084_Eistla_region_pancake_volcanoes.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PIA00084_Eistla_region_pancake_volcanoes.jpg)

Radar mosaic of two [pancake domes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pancake_dome "Pancake dome") in Venus's Eistla region—both 65 km (40 mi) wide and less than 1 km (0.62 mi) high

Much of the Venusian surface appears to have been shaped by volcanic activity. Venus has several times as many volcanoes as Earth, and it has 167 large volcanoes that are over 100 km (60 mi) across. The only volcanic complex of this size on Earth is the [Big Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii_(island) "Hawaii (island)") of Hawaii.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Frankel-46): 154  More than 85,000 volcanoes on Venus have been identified and mapped.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-56)[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-57) This is not because Venus is more volcanically active than Earth, but because its crust is older and is not subject to the [erosion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erosion "Erosion") processes active on Earth. Earth's [oceanic crust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceanic_crust "Oceanic crust") is continually recycled by [subduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subduction "Subduction") at the boundaries of tectonic plates, and has an average age of about 100 million years,[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Karttunen_et_al_2007-58) whereas the Venusian surface is estimated to be 300–600 million years old.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nimmo98-44)[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Frankel-46)

Several lines of evidence point to ongoing [volcanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic "Volcanic") activity on Venus. Sulfur dioxide concentrations in the upper atmosphere dropped by a factor of 10 between 1978 and 1986, jumped in 2006, and again declined 10-fold.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ESA_2012-12-03-59) This may mean that levels were boosted several times by large volcanic eruptions.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Glaze_1999-60)[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Marcq2012-61) It has been suggested that Venusian lightning (discussed below) could originate from volcanic activity (i.e. [volcanic lightning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanic_lightning "Volcanic lightning")). In January 2020, astronomers reported evidence suggesting that Venus is currently volcanically active, specifically the detection of [olivine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olivine "Olivine"), a volcanic product that would weather quickly on the planet's surface.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NYT-20200109-62)[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-SCI-20200103-63)

This massive volcanic activity is fuelled by a hot interior, which models say could be explained by energetic collisions when the planet was young, as well as [radioactive decay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radioactive_decay "Radioactive decay") as in the case of the earth. Impacts would have had significantly higher velocity than on Earth, both because Venus moves faster due to its closer proximity to the Sun and because high-eccentricity objects colliding with the planet would have high speeds.[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-64)

In 2008 and 2009, the first direct evidence for ongoing volcanism was observed by _Venus Express_, in the form of four transient localized infrared hot spots within the rift zone [Ganis Chasma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganis_Chasma "Ganis Chasma"),[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-USGS_Ganis_Chasma-65)[[note 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-67) near the shield volcano [Maat Mons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maat_Mons "Maat Mons"). Three of the spots were observed in more than one successive orbit. These spots are thought to represent lava freshly released by volcanic eruptions.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lakdawalla2015-66)[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ESA_2015-06-18-68) The actual temperatures are not known, because the size of the hot spots could not be measured, but are likely to have been in the 800–1,100 K (527–827°C; 980–1,520°F) range, relative to a normal temperature of 740 K (467°C; 872°F).[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Shalygin2015-69) In 2023, scientists reexamined topographical images of the Maat Mons region taken by the _[Magellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan\_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)")_ orbiter. Using computer simulations, they determined that the topography had changed during an 8-month interval, and concluded that active volcanism was the cause.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-70)

#### Craters

[![Image 9: The plains of Venus](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/PIA00103_Venus_-_3-D_Perspective_View_of_Lavinia_Planitia.jpg/250px-PIA00103_Venus_-_3-D_Perspective_View_of_Lavinia_Planitia.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PIA00103_Venus_-_3-D_Perspective_View_of_Lavinia_Planitia.jpg)

[Impact craters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_crater "Impact crater") on the surface of Venus (false-colour, [3D projection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3D_projection "3D projection") image reconstructed from radar data)

There are almost a thousand impact craters on Venus, evenly distributed across its surface. On other cratered bodies, such as Earth and the Moon, craters show a range of states of degradation. On the Moon, degradation is caused by subsequent impacts, whereas on Earth it is caused by wind and rain erosion. On Venus, about 85% of the craters are in pristine condition. The number of craters, together with their well-preserved condition, indicates the planet underwent a global resurfacing event 300–600 million years ago,[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nimmo98-44)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Strom1994-45) followed by a decay in volcanism.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Romeo_Turcotte_2018-71) Whereas Earth's crust is in continuous motion, Venus is thought to be unable to sustain such a process. Without plate tectonics to dissipate heat from its mantle, Venus instead undergoes a cyclical process in which mantle temperatures rise until they reach a critical level that weakens the crust. Then, over a period of about 100 million years, subduction occurs on an enormous scale, completely recycling the crust.[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Frankel-46)

Venusian craters range from 3 to 280 km (2 to 174 mi) in diameter. No craters are smaller than 3 km, because of the effects of the dense atmosphere on incoming objects. Objects with less than a certain [kinetic energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinetic_energy "Kinetic energy") are slowed so much by the atmosphere that they do not create an impact crater.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Herrick_Phillips_1993-72) Incoming projectiles less than 50 m (160 ft) in diameter will fragment and burn up in the atmosphere before reaching the ground.[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Morrison_Owens_2003-73)

### Internal structure

[![Image 10: Spherical cross-section of Venus showing the different layers](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/InteriorOfVenus.svg/330px-InteriorOfVenus.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:InteriorOfVenus.svg)

The [differentiated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_differentiation "Planetary differentiation") structure of Venus

Without data from [reflection seismology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reflection_seismology "Reflection seismology") or knowledge of its [moment of inertia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moment_of_inertia "Moment of inertia"), little direct information has been available about the internal structure and [geochemistry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geochemistry "Geochemistry") of Venus.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-goettel-74) The similarity in size and density between Venus and Earth suggests that they share a similar internal structure: a [core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_core "Planetary core"), [mantle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mantle_(geology) "Mantle (geology)"), and [crust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crust_(geology) "Crust (geology)"). Like that of Earth, the Venusian core is most likely at least partially liquid because the two planets have been cooling at about the same rate,[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Faure_Mensing_2007-75) although a completely solid core cannot be ruled out.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dumoulin2017-76) The slightly smaller size of Venus means pressures are 24% lower in its deep interior than Earth's.[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Aitta_2016-77) The predicted values for the moment of inertia based on planetary models suggest a core radius of 2,900–3,450 km.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dumoulin2017-76) There is now an estimate of 3,500 km from the [moment of inertia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moment_of_inertia "Moment of inertia") based on the rate of [axial precession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axial_precession "Axial precession"), measured between 2006 and 2020.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Margot_et_al_2021-12)[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-O'Callaghan_2021-78)

The crust of Venus is estimated to be 40 kilometers thick on average and at most 65 kilometers thick.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-79)

The principal difference between the two planets is the lack of evidence for plate tectonics on Venus, possibly because its crust is too strong to [subduct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subduct "Subduct") without water to make it less [viscous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viscous "Viscous"). This results in reduced heat loss from the planet, preventing it from cooling and providing a likely explanation for its lack of an internally generated [magnetic field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_field "Magnetic field").[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nimmo_2002-80) Instead, Venus may lose its internal heat in periodic major resurfacing events.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nimmo98-44)

### Magnetic field and core

[![Image 11](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Venusian_magnetosphere.svg/250px-Venusian_magnetosphere.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venusian_magnetosphere.svg)

Venus interacts with the solar wind. Components of the induced magnetosphere are shown.

In 1967, _[Venera 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_4 "Venera 4")_ found Venus's [magnetic field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetic_field "Magnetic field") to be much weaker than that of Earth. This magnetic field is induced by an interaction between the [ionosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionosphere "Ionosphere") and the [solar wind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind"),[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Eroshenko_et_al_1969-81)[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kivelson_Russell_1995-82)[_[page needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] rather than by an internal [dynamo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamo_theory "Dynamo theory") as in the Earth's [core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_core "Planetary core"). [Venus's small induced magnetosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnetosphere_of_Venus "Magnetosphere of Venus") provides negligible protection to the atmosphere against [solar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_radiation "Solar radiation") and [cosmic radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmic_radiation "Cosmic radiation").

The lack of an intrinsic magnetic field on Venus was surprising, given that it is similar to Earth in size and was expected to contain a dynamo at its core. A dynamo requires three things: a [conducting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrical_conductor "Electrical conductor") liquid, rotation, and [convection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convection "Convection"). The core is thought to be electrically conductive and, although its rotation is often thought to be too slow, simulations show it is adequate to produce a dynamo.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Luhmann_Russell_2006-83)[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Stevenson_2003-84) This implies that the dynamo is missing because of a lack of convection in Venus's core. On Earth, convection occurs in the liquid outer layer of the core because the bottom of the liquid layer is much higher in temperature than the top. On Venus, a global resurfacing event may have shut down plate tectonics and led to a reduced [heat flux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_flux "Heat flux") through the crust. This [insulating](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_insulation "Thermal insulation") effect would cause the mantle temperature to increase, thereby reducing the heat flux out of the core. As a result, no internal geodynamo is available to drive a magnetic field. Instead, the heat from the core is reheating the crust.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-nimmo02-85)

One possibility is that Venus has no solid inner core,[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Konopliv_Yoder_1996-86) or that its core is not cooling, so that the entire liquid part of the core is at approximately the same temperature. Another possibility is that its core has already been completely solidified. The state of the core is highly dependent on the concentration of [sulphur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulphur "Sulphur"), which is unknown at present.[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-nimmo02-85)

Another possibility is that the absence of a large impact on Venus (_contra_ the Earth's "Moon-forming" impact) left the core of Venus stratified from the core's incremental formation, and without the forces to initiate/sustain convection, and thus a "geodynamo".[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Jacobsen2017-87)

The weak magnetosphere around Venus means that the solar wind interacts directly with its outer atmosphere. Here, ions of hydrogen and oxygen are being created by the [dissociation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissociation_(chemistry) "Dissociation (chemistry)") of water molecules due to [ultraviolet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet") radiation. The solar wind then supplies energy that gives some of these ions sufficient speed to escape Venus's gravity field. This erosion process results in a steady loss of low-mass hydrogen, helium, and oxygen ions, whereas higher-mass molecules, such as carbon dioxide, are more likely to be retained. Atmospheric erosion by the solar wind could have led to the loss of most of Venus's water during the first billion years after it formed.[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-nature450_7170_629-88) However, the planet may have retained a dynamo for its first 2–3 billion years, so the water loss may have occurred more recently.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-O'Rourke_et_al_2019-89) The erosion has increased the ratio of higher-mass [deuterium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deuterium "Deuterium") to lower-mass hydrogen in the atmosphere 100 times compared to the rest of the solar system.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Donahue_et_al_1982-90)

Atmosphere and climate
----------------------

[![Image 12: The atmosphere of Venus appears darker and lined with shadows. The shadows trace the prevailing wind direction.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Venus_-_December_23_2016.png/250px-Venus_-_December_23_2016.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_-_December_23_2016.png)

Cloud structure of the Venusian atmosphere, made visible through [ultraviolet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet") imaging

Venus has a dense [atmosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere "Atmosphere") composed of 96.5% [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide"), 3.5% nitrogen—both exist as supercritical fluids at the planet's surface with a density 6.5% that of water[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-u3r1a-91)—and traces of other gases including [sulphur dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulphur_dioxide "Sulphur dioxide").[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-SolarSystemEncyclopedia-92) The mass of its atmosphere is 92 times that of Earth's, whereas the pressure at its surface is about 93 times that at Earth's—a pressure equivalent to that at a depth of nearly 1 km (5⁄8 mi) under Earth's ocean surfaces. The density at the surface is 65 kg/m 3 (4.1 lb/cu ft), 6.5% that of water[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-u3r1a-91) or 50 times as dense as Earth's atmosphere at 293 K (20°C; 68°F) at sea level. The CO 2-rich atmosphere generates the strongest [greenhouse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_effect "Greenhouse effect") in the Solar System, creating surface temperatures of at least 735 K (462°C; 864°F).[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-nasa_venus-93)[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-CWRU_2006-94) This makes the Venusian surface hotter than [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)")'s, which has a minimum surface temperature of 53 K (−220°C; −364°F) and maximum surface temperature of 700 K (427°C; 801°F),[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lewis_2004-95)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Prockter_2005-96) even though Venus is nearly twice Mercury's distance from the Sun and thus receives only around a quarter of Mercury's solar [irradiance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irradiance "Irradiance"), of 2,600 W/m 2 (double that of Earth).[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4) Because of its [runaway greenhouse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Runaway_greenhouse_effect "Runaway greenhouse effect"), Venus has been identified by scientists such as [Carl Sagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Sagan "Carl Sagan") as a warning and research object linked to [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") on Earth.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Newitz_2013-31) Therefore Venus has been called a greenhouse planet,[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-a490-97) a planet under a greenhouse inferno.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-p181-98)

Venus temperature[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Weather-99)| Type | Surface temperature |
| --- | --- |
| Maximum | 900°F (482°C) |
| Normal | 847°F (453°C) |
| Minimum | 820°F (438°C) |

Venus's atmosphere is rich in primordial [noble gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Noble_gas "Noble gas") compared to that of Earth.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Halliday_2020-100) This enrichment indicates an early divergence from Earth in evolution. An unusually large comet impact[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Owen_et_al_1992-101) or accretion of a more massive [primary atmosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_atmosphere "Primary atmosphere") from the solar nebula[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Pepin_1991-102) have been proposed to explain the enrichment. However, the atmosphere is poor in radiogenic [argon-40](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argon-40 "Argon-40"), a proxy for mantle degassing, suggesting an early shutdown of major magmatism.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Namiki_Solomon_1998-103)[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-O'Rurke_Korenaga_2015-104)

Studies have suggested that billions of years ago, the atmosphere of Venus may have been much more like the one surrounding the early Earth, and there may have been substantial quantities of liquid water on the surface.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Ernst_2022-105)[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Way_Del_Genio_2020_p.-106)[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Way_Del_Genio_Kiang_Sohl_2016_pp._8376%E2%80%938383-107) After a period of 600 million to several billion years,[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-baas39_540-108) the rising luminosity of the Sun and possibly [large volcanic resurfacing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Large_igneous_province "Large igneous province") caused the evaporation of the original water.[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Steigerwald_2022-109) A runaway greenhouse effect was created once a critical level of greenhouse gases (including water) was reached in the atmosphere.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kasting-110) Although the surface conditions on Venus are no longer hospitable to any terrestrial-like life that might have formed before this event, there is speculation that life may exist in the upper cloud layers of Venus, 50 km (30 mi) above the surface, where atmospheric conditions are the most Earth-like in the Solar System,[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Tillman_2018-111) with temperatures ranging between 303 and 353 K (30 and 80°C; 86 and 176°F), and the pressure and radiation being about the same as at Earth's surface, but with acidic clouds and the carbon dioxide air.[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mullen_2002-112)[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Landis_2003-113)[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cockell1999-114) More specifically, between heights of 48 and 59 km temperature and radiation conditions are suitable for life. At lower elevations water would evaporate and at higher elevation UV radiation would be too strong.[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Patel_Mason_Nordheim_Dartnell_2022_p=114796-115)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Herbst_Banjac_Atri_Nordheim_2019_p=A15-116) The putative detection of an [absorption line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Absorption_line "Absorption line") of [phosphine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phosphine "Phosphine") in Venus's atmosphere, with no known pathway for abiotic production, led to speculation in September 2020 that there could be extant life currently present in the atmosphere.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Drake_2020-117)[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Greaves_et_al_2020-118) Later research attributed the spectroscopic signal that was interpreted as phosphine to sulphur dioxide,[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lincowski_et_al_2021-119) or found that in fact there was no absorption line.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Beall_2020-120)[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Snellan_et_al_2020-121)

[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/11214_2023_956_Fig6_HTML.webp/250px-11214_2023_956_Fig6_HTML.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:11214_2023_956_Fig6_HTML.webp)

Atmospheric profile by altitude (left scale): cloud layers, temperature change (_VIRA_ thick line and bottom scale), pressure change (right scale) and wind speed (_PV_ dotted lines and top scale)

[Thermal inertia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thermal_inertia "Thermal inertia") and the transfer of heat by winds in the lower atmosphere mean that the surface temperature does not vary significantly between the hemispheres facing and not facing the Sun, despite Venus's slow rotation. Winds at the surface are slow, moving at a few kilometres per hour, but because of the high density of the atmosphere at the surface, they exert a significant amount of force against obstructions, and transport dust and small stones across the surface. This alone would make it difficult for a human to walk through, even without the heat, pressure, and lack of oxygen.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Moshkin_et_al_1979-122)

Above the dense CO 2 layer are thick clouds 45 to 70 km above the surface,[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-123) consisting mainly of [sulphuric acid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulphuric_acid "Sulphuric acid"), which is formed by a reaction catalyzed by UV radiation from sulphur dioxide molecules and then water,[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-124) resulting in sulphuric acid hydrate.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-125) Additionally, the clouds contain approximately 1% [ferric chloride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferric_chloride "Ferric chloride").[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-kras006-126)[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Krasnopolsky_2006-127) Other possible constituents of the cloud particles are [ferric sulfate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferric_sulfate "Ferric sulfate"), [aluminium chloride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aluminium_chloride "Aluminium chloride") and [phosphoric anhydride](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phosphoric_anhydride "Phosphoric anhydride"). Clouds at different levels have different compositions and particle size distributions.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-kras006-126) These clouds reflect, like thick cloud cover on Earth, about 70% of the sunlight that falls on them back into space,[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Davis_2021-128) and since they cover the whole planet they prevent visual observation of the surface. The permanent cloud cover means that although Venus is closer than Earth to the Sun, it receives less sunlight on the ground, with only 10% of the received sunlight reaching the surface,[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ESA_Blog_Navigator_%E2%80%93_Navigator_page_for_active_ESA_blogs_2012-129) resulting in average daytime levels of illumination at the surface of 14,000 [lux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lux "Lux"), comparable to that on Earth "in the daytime with overcast clouds"[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-sci_news_1976-130).

Venus's atmosphere rotates much faster than its solid body, a phenomenon known as atmospheric [super-rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmospheric_super-rotation "Atmospheric super-rotation").[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-131) This results in strong 300 km/h (185 mph) winds at the cloud tops, which complete a full rotation around the planet in about 4 days, corresponding to 60 times the speed of the planet's rotation[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Rossow_et_al_1990-132), whereas Earth's strongest winds reach only 10–20% of its rotational speed.

Although Venus looks featureless in visible light, there are bands or streaks in the UV, whose origin has not been pinned down. The absorption of UV may be due to a compound of oxygen and sulfur, OSSO, which has a double bond between the sulfur atoms and exists in "cis" and "trans" forms, or due to polysulfur compounds from S 2 to S 8.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-133)

The surface of Venus is effectively [isothermal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isothermal "Isothermal"); it retains a constant temperature not only between the two hemispheres but between the equator and the poles.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4)[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lorenz_et_al_2001-134) Venus's minute [axial tilt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axial_tilt "Axial tilt")—less than 3°, compared to 23° on Earth—also minimizes seasonal temperature variation.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NASA_Seasons-135) Altitude is one of the few factors that affect Venusian temperatures. The highest point on Venus, [Maxwell Montes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell_Montes "Maxwell Montes"), is therefore the coolest point on Venus, with a temperature of about 655 K (380°C; 715°F) and an atmospheric pressure of about 4.5 MPa (45 bar).[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Basilevsky_2003-136)[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-McGill_2010-137) In 1995, the [_Magellan_ spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)") imaged a highly reflective substance at the tops of the highest mountain peaks, a "[Venus snow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_snow "Venus snow")" that bore a strong resemblance to terrestrial snow. This substance likely formed by a similar process to snow, albeit at a far higher temperature. Too volatile to condense on the surface, it rose in gaseous form to higher elevations, where it is cooler and could precipitate. The identity of this substance is not known with certainty, but speculation has ranged from elemental [tellurium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tellurium "Tellurium") to lead sulfide ([galena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galena "Galena")).[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Otten_2004-138)

Although Venus has no seasons, in 2019 astronomers identified a cyclical variation in sunlight absorption by the atmosphere, possibly caused by opaque, absorbing particles suspended in the upper clouds. The variation causes observed changes in the speed of Venus's zonal winds and appears to rise and fall in time with the Sun's 11-year [sunspot cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunspot_cycle "Sunspot cycle").[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-TAJ-20190826-139)

The existence of lightning in the atmosphere of Venus has been controversial[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lorentz_2018-140) since the first suspected bursts were detected by the Soviet [Venera probes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera "Venera").[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kranopol'skii_1980-141)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Russell,_Philips-142)[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Venera_12-143) In 2006–07, _[Venus Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus\_Express "Venus Express")_ clearly detected [whistler mode waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electromagnetic_electron_wave#R_wave_and_L_wave "Electromagnetic electron wave"), the signatures of lightning. Their [intermittent](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/intermittent "wikt:intermittent") appearance indicates a pattern associated with weather activity. According to these measurements, the lightning rate is at least half that on Earth,[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Russell_2007-144) however other instruments have not detected lightning at all.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lorentz_2018-140) The origin of any lightning remains unclear, but could originate from clouds or [Venusian volcanoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volcanism_on_Venus "Volcanism on Venus").

In 2007, _Venus Express_ discovered that a huge double [atmospheric polar vortex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_vortex "Polar vortex") exists at the south pole.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hand_2007-145)[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-BBC_2007_11_28-146)_Venus Express_ discovered, in 2011, that an [ozone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ozone "Ozone") layer exists high in the atmosphere of Venus.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-esaozone-147) In 2013 [ESA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESA "ESA") scientists reported that the [ionosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionosphere "Ionosphere") of Venus streams outwards in a manner similar to "the ion tail seen streaming from a [comet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comet "Comet") under similar conditions."[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ESA-20130129-148)[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Space-20130130-149)

In December 2015, and to a lesser extent in April and May 2016, researchers working on Japan's _Akatsuki_ mission observed bow-shaped objects in the atmosphere of Venus. This was considered direct evidence of the existence of perhaps the largest stationary [gravity waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_wave "Gravity wave") in the solar system.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Fukuhara_et_al_2017-150)[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Rincon_2017-151)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Chang_2017-152)

Colour and sound[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-l172-153) of the atmosphere at the surface have been recorded, with [the sky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterrestrial_sky#Venus "Extraterrestrial sky") having an orange-yellow colour, while at higher altitudes being white.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-t069-48)

Orbit and rotation
------------------

[![Image 14: Mars circling the Sun further and slower than Earth](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif/330px-Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_system_orrery_inner_planets.gif)

Venus is the second planet from the Sun, making a full orbit in about 224 days.

Venus orbits the Sun at an average distance of about 0.72[AU](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit "Astronomical unit") (108 million[km](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kilometre "Kilometre"); 67 million[mi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mile "Mile")), and completes an orbit every 224.7 days. It completes 13 orbits in 7.998 years, so its position in our sky almost repeats every eight years. Although all planetary [orbits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbit "Orbit") are [elliptical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellipse "Ellipse"), Venus's orbit is currently the closest to circular, with an [eccentricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity") of less than 0.01.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4) Simulations of the early solar system orbital dynamics have shown that the eccentricity of the Venus orbit may have been substantially larger in the past, reaching values as high as 0.31 and possibly impacting early climate evolution.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-psj_1_42-154)

[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/11214_2023_956_Fig7_HTML.webp/330px-11214_2023_956_Fig7_HTML.webp.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:11214_2023_956_Fig7_HTML.webp)

Venus and its rotation in respect to its revolution

Venus has [retrograde rotation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retrograde_rotation "Retrograde rotation"), meaning that unlike most planets including Earth it rotates clockwise around its own axis, opposite to its [anticlockwise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anticlockwise "Anticlockwise") rotation around the Sun. Therefore Venusian [sidereal day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidereal_day "Sidereal day"), 243 Earth days, lasts longer than a Venusian year, 224.7 Earth days. If Venus were [tidally locked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_lock "Tidal lock") to the Sun, it would always have the same face pointed to the Sun and its sidereal day would be 224.7 days. However, Venus's atmosphere is massive and it is close to the Sun, so differential heating of the atmosphere gives Venus a small retrograde rotation. The day length also fluctuates by up to 20 minutes for the same reason.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-EarthSky_Updates_on_your_cosmos_and_world_2021-155)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-156) Venus's rotation period measured with _Magellan_ spacecraft data over a 500-day period is smaller than the rotation period measured during the 16-year period between the Magellan spacecraft and _Venus Express_ visits, with a difference of about 6.5 minutes.[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-slowing_spin-157) Because of the retrograde rotation, the length of a [solar day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_day "Solar day") on Venus is significantly shorter than the sidereal day, at 116.75 Earth days.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-planetary-facts-11) One Venusian year is about 1.92 Venusian solar days.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-compare-158) To an observer on the surface of Venus, the Sun would rise in [the west](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poles_of_astronomical_bodies "Poles of astronomical bodies") and set in the east,[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-compare-158) although Venus's opaque clouds prevent observing the Sun from the planet's surface.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Brunier_2002-159)

Venus may have formed from the [solar nebula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_nebula "Solar nebula") with a different rotation period and obliquity, reaching its current state because of chaotic spin changes caused by planetary perturbations and [tidal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tide "Tide") effects on its dense atmosphere, a change that would have occurred over the course of billions of years. The rotation period of Venus may represent an equilibrium state between tidal locking to the Sun's gravitation, which tends to slow rotation, and an atmospheric tide created by solar heating of the thick Venusian atmosphere.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Correia_et_al_2003-160)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Laskar_De_Surgy_2003-161) The 584-day average interval between successive close approaches to Earth is almost exactly equal to 5 Venusian solar days (5.001444 to be precise),[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Gold_Soter_1969-162) but the hypothesis of a spin-orbit resonance with Earth has been discounted.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-apj2_230_L123-163)

Venus has no natural satellites.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-icarus202-164) It has several [trojan asteroids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trojan_asteroid "Trojan asteroid"): the [quasi-satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quasi-satellite "Quasi-satellite")[524522 Zoozve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/524522_Zoozve "524522 Zoozve")[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mikkola_et_al_2004-165)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Carlos_De_la_Fuente_Marcos_2012-166) and two other temporary trojans, [2001 CK 32](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/(322756)_2001_CK32 "(322756) 2001 CK32") and [2012 XE 133](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_XE133 "2012 XE133").[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-dynamics-167) In the 17th century, [Giovanni Cassini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Cassini "Giovanni Cassini") reported a moon orbiting Venus, which was named [Neith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neith_(hypothetical_moon) "Neith (hypothetical moon)") and numerous sightings were reported over the following 200 years, but most were determined to be stars in the vicinity. Alex Alemi's and [David Stevenson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_J._Stevenson "David J. Stevenson")'s 2006 study of models of the early Solar System at the [California Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology "California Institute of Technology") shows Venus likely had at least one moon created by a huge [impact event](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impact_event "Impact event") billions of years ago.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Musser_2006-168) About 10 million years later, according to the study, another impact reversed the planet's spin direction and the resulting [tidal deceleration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_deceleration "Tidal deceleration") caused the Venusian moon gradually to spiral inward until it collided with Venus.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Tytell_2006-169) If later impacts created moons, these were removed in the same way. An alternative explanation for the lack of satellites is the effect of strong solar tides, which can destabilize large satellites orbiting the inner terrestrial planets.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-icarus202-164)

The orbital space of Venus has a [dust ring-cloud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_dust#Rings_of_dust "Interplanetary dust"),[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Frazier_2021-170) with a suspected origin either from Venus–trailing asteroids,[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Garner_2019-171) interplanetary dust migrating in waves, or the remains of the Solar System's original [circumstellar disc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumstellar_disc "Circumstellar disc") that formed the [planetary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_system "Planetary system").[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Rehm_2021-172)

### Orbit in respect to Earth

[![Image 16: A complex, spiral, floral pattern with five loops encircling the middle](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Venus_pentagram.png/250px-Venus_pentagram.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_pentagram.png)

Earth is positioned at the centre of the diagram, and the curve represents the direction and distance of Venus as a function of time.

Earth and Venus have a near [orbital resonance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbital_resonance "Orbital resonance") of 13:8 (Earth orbits eight times for every 13 orbits of Venus).[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Bazs%C3%B3-173) Therefore, they approach each other and reach [inferior conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_conjunction "Inferior conjunction") in [synodic periods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synodic_period "Synodic period") of 584 days, on average.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4) The path that Venus makes in relation to Earth viewed geocentrically draws a [pentagram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentagram#Pentagram_of_Venus "Pentagram") over five synodic periods, shifting every period by 144°. This pentagram of Venus is sometimes referred to as the petals of Venus due to the path's visual similarity to a flower.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Ottewel_2022-174)

When Venus lies between Earth and the Sun in [inferior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy)#Superior_and_inferior "Conjunction (astronomy)") conjunction, it makes the closest approach to Earth of any planet at an average distance of 41 million km (25 million mi).[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4)[[note 2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-176)[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-MoreOrLess-175) Because of the [decreasing eccentricity of Earth's orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milankovitch_cycles#Orbital_eccentricity "Milankovitch cycles"), the minimum distances will become greater over tens of thousands of years. From the year 1 to 5383, there are 526 approaches less than 40 million km (25 million mi); then, there are none for about 60,158 years.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Solex11-177)

While Venus approaches Earth the closest, Mercury is more often the closest to Earth of all planets and to any other planet.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-AIP_Publishing_2019_p.-178)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-179) Venus has been used as a waypoint for [gravity assist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist") maneuvers, which has been identified as a faster and economic way to travel to Mercury,[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-180)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-181) the Sun,[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-182) asteroids,[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-183) Mars,[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-184) Jupiter and beyond.[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Petropoulos_Longuski_Bonfiglio_2000_pp._776%E2%80%93783-185)[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Taylor_2020-186)

Tidally Venus exerts the third strongest [tidal force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force") on Earth, after the Moon and the Sun, though significantly less.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Science_Mission_Directorate_2000-187)

Observability
-------------

[![Image 17: A photograph of the night sky taken from the seashore. A glimmer of sunlight is on the horizon. There are many stars visible. Venus is at the centre, much brighter than any of the stars, and its light can be seen reflected in the ocean.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Venus-pacific-levelled.jpg/250px-Venus-pacific-levelled.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus-pacific-levelled.jpg)

Venus, pictured centre-right, is always brighter than all other planets or stars at their maximal brightness, as seen from Earth. Jupiter is visible at the top of the image.

To the [naked eye](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naked_eye "Naked eye"), Venus appears as a white point of light with a maximum [apparent magnitude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparent_magnitude "Apparent magnitude") of −4.92 brighter than any other planet or star apart from the Sun,[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dickinson_1998-188) even when faintest during [its transit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus "Transit of Venus") with an apparent magnitude of −2.98.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mallama_and_Hilton-20) The planet's mean apparent magnitude is −4.14 with a standard deviation of 0.31.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mallama_and_Hilton-20) The brightest magnitude occurs during the crescent phase about one month before or after an inferior conjunction. Venus fades to about magnitude −3 when it is backlit by the Sun, although the exact value depends on the [phase angle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phase_angle_(astronomy) "Phase angle (astronomy)").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-n850-189) The planet is bright enough to be seen in broad daylight,[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Flanders_2011-190) but is more easily visible when the Sun is low on the horizon or setting. As an [inferior planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_planet "Inferior planet"), it always lies within about 47° of the [Sun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun "Sun").[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ephemeris-191)

Venus "overtakes" Earth every 584 days as it orbits the Sun.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-fact-4) As it does so, it changes from the "Evening Star", visible after sunset, to the "Morning Star", visible before sunrise. Although Mercury, the other inferior planet, reaches a maximum elongation of only 28° and is often difficult to discern in twilight, Venus is hard to miss when it is at its brightest. Its greater maximum elongation means it is visible in dark skies long after sunset. As the brightest point-like object in the sky, Venus is a commonly misreported "[unidentified flying object](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unidentified_flying_object "Unidentified flying object")".[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ASP_2021-192)

Because Venus comes close to the earth at [inferior conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_conjunction "Inferior conjunction") and has an orbit inclined to the plane of the earth's orbit, it can appear more than 8° north or south of the [ecliptic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecliptic "Ecliptic"), more than any other planet or the moon. Every eight years around March it appears this far north of the ecliptic, in [Pisces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pisces_(constellation) "Pisces (constellation)") (such as in mid-March 2025), and every eight years it appears this far south of the ecliptic in August or September in [Virgo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgo_(constellation) "Virgo (constellation)") (as in late August 2023). Venus can thus be north of the sun and appear as a morning star and an evening star on the same day, in the northern hemisphere. The timing of these north or south excursions gets slowly earlier in the year, and over 30 cycles (240 years) the cycle is gradually replaced by another cycle offset by three years, so the situation returns close to the original situation after 243 orbits of Earth, 395 of Venus.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-193)

[Lunar occultations of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_occultation_of_Venus "Lunar occultation of Venus"), in which the moon blocks the view of Venus for observers in certain parts of the earth, occur on average about twice a year, sometimes several times in a year (though rarely).

### Phases

[![Image 18: Diagram illustrating the phases of Venus](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Phases_Venus.jpg/250px-Phases_Venus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phases_Venus.jpg)

The phases of Venus and evolution of its apparent diameter

As it orbits the Sun, Venus displays [phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phases_of_Venus "Phases of Venus") like those of the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") in a [telescopic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_telescope "Optical telescope") view. The planet appears as a small and "full" disc when it is on the opposite side of the Sun (at superior [conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy) "Conjunction (astronomy)")). Venus shows a larger disc and "quarter phase" at its maximum [elongations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elongation_(astronomy) "Elongation (astronomy)") from the Sun, and appears at its brightest in the night sky. The planet presents a much larger thin "crescent" in telescopic views as it passes along the near side between Earth and the Sun. Venus displays its largest size and "new phase" when it is between Earth and the Sun (at inferior conjunction). Its atmosphere is visible through telescopes by the halo of sunlight refracted around it.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ephemeris-191) The phases are clearly visible in a 4" telescope.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-194) Although naked eye visibility of Venus's phases is disputed, records exist of observations of its crescent.[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Goines_1995-195)

### Daylight apparitions

[![Image 19: venus next to a crescent moon in the blue daytime sky](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Lunar_Occultation_of_Venus_%28NHQ201512070001%29.jpg/250px-Lunar_Occultation_of_Venus_%28NHQ201512070001%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lunar_Occultation_of_Venus_(NHQ201512070001).jpg)

Venus is often visible to the naked eye in daytime, as seen just prior to the lunar occultation of 7 December 2015.

When Venus is sufficiently bright with enough angular distance from the sun, it is easily observed in a clear daytime sky with the naked eye, though most people do not know to look for it.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-196) Astronomer [Edmund Halley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Halley "Edmund Halley") calculated its maximum naked eye brightness in 1716, when many Londoners were alarmed by its appearance in the daytime. French emperor [Napoleon Bonaparte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte "Napoleon Bonaparte") once witnessed a daytime apparition of the planet while at a reception in [Luxembourg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourg "Luxembourg").[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Chatfield_2015-197) Another historical daytime observation of the planet took place during the inauguration of the American president [Abraham Lincoln](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln "Abraham Lincoln") in Washington, D.C., on 4 March 1865.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Gaherty_2012-198)

### Transits

[![Image 20: White disk with a small black dot projected on a screen](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Transit_of_Venus_viewed_in_Wagga_Wagga_%282%29.jpg/250px-Transit_of_Venus_viewed_in_Wagga_Wagga_%282%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Transit_of_Venus_viewed_in_Wagga_Wagga_(2).jpg)

[2012 transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_transit_of_Venus "2012 transit of Venus"), projected by a [telescope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telescope "Telescope") onto a white card

A [transit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_(astronomy) "Transit (astronomy)") of Venus is the appearance of Venus in front of the Sun, during [inferior conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_conjunction "Inferior conjunction"). Since the orbit of Venus is slightly inclined relative to Earth's orbit, most inferior conjunctions with Earth, which occur every [synodic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synodic_period "Synodic period") of 1.6 years, do not produce a transit of Venus. Consequently, Venus transits only occur when an inferior conjunction takes place during some days of June or December, when the orbits of Venus and Earth cross a straight line with the Sun.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NASA_2004-199) This results in Venus transiting above Earth in a sequence currently of 8 years, 105.5 years, 8 years and 121.5 years, forming cycles of 243 years.

Historically, transits of Venus were important, because they allowed astronomers to determine the size of the [astronomical unit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_unit "Astronomical unit"), and hence the size of the Solar System as shown by [Jeremiah Horrocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks "Jeremiah Horrocks") in [1639 with the first known observation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus,_1639 "Transit of Venus, 1639") of a Venus transit (after history's first observed planetary [transit in 1631, of Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Mercury "Transit of Mercury")).[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kollerstrom_1998-200)

Only seven Venus transits have been observed so far, since their occurrences were calculated in the 1621 by [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler"). [Captain Cook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain_Cook "Captain Cook") sailed to [Tahiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tahiti "Tahiti") in 1768 to record the third observed transit of Venus, which subsequently resulted in the exploration of the east coast of Australia.[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hornsby_1771-201)[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Woolley_1969-202)

The latest pair was [June 8, 2004](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus,_2004 "Transit of Venus, 2004") and [June 5–6, 2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus,_2012 "Transit of Venus, 2012"). The transit could be watched live from many online outlets or observed locally with the right equipment and conditions.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Boyle_2016-203) The preceding pair of transits occurred in [December 1874](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus,_1874 "Transit of Venus, 1874") and [December 1882](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus,_1882 "Transit of Venus, 1882").

The next transit will occur in December 2117 and December 2125.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Espenak_2004-204)

### Ashen light

[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Venus-ParkerSolarProbe-July2020.jpg/250px-Venus-ParkerSolarProbe-July2020.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus-ParkerSolarProbe-July2020.jpg)

[Nightglow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nightglow "Nightglow") is since 2022 considered the most likely candidate for the ashen light. In this visible light near-infrared image it is most discernable as a bright line along the limb of Venus.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-e367-205) The surface and its features, like the visible dark patch in this image, the [Ovda Regio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovda_Regio "Ovda Regio") plateau of [Aphrodite Terra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphrodite_Terra "Aphrodite Terra"), is much less discernable by the human eye, though reportedly seen by some people, possibly due to higher sensitivity in the spectrum that the surface glows.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-n420-206)

A long-standing mystery of Venus observations is the so-called [ashen light](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashen_light "Ashen light")—an apparent weak illumination of its dark side, seen when the planet is in the crescent phase. The first claimed observation of ashen light was made in 1643, but the existence of the illumination has never been reliably confirmed. Observers have speculated it may result from electrical activity in the Venusian atmosphere, but it could be illusory, resulting from the physiological effect of observing a bright, crescent-shaped object.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Baum_2000-207)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Russell,_Philips-142) The ashen light has often been sighted when Venus is in the evening sky, when the evening terminator of the planet is towards Earth.

Observation and exploration history
-----------------------------------

### Early observation

Venus is in Earth's sky bright enough to be visible [without aid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naked_eye "Naked eye"), making it one of the [classical planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_planets "Classical planets") that human cultures have known and identified throughout history, particularly for being the third brightest object in Earth's sky after the Sun and the Moon.
