Because the movements of Venus appear to be discontinuous (it disappears due to its proximity to the sun, for many days at a time, and then reappears on the other horizon), some cultures did not recognize Venus as a single entity;[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) instead, they assumed it to be two separate stars on each horizon: the morning and evening star.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) Nonetheless, a [cylinder seal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cylinder_seal "Cylinder seal") from the [Jemdet Nasr period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jemdet_Nasr_period "Jemdet Nasr period") and the [Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_tablet_of_Ammisaduqa "Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa") from the [First Babylonian dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Babylonian_dynasty "First Babylonian dynasty") indicate that the ancient Sumerians already knew that the morning and evening stars were the same celestial object.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Sachs_1974-209)[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hobson_2009-210)

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Venus_Tablet_of_Ammisaduqa.jpg/250px-Venus_Tablet_of_Ammisaduqa.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_Tablet_of_Ammisaduqa.jpg)

Oldest known recording of Venus positions, on the [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia")_[Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus\_tablet\_of\_Ammisaduqa "Venus tablet of Ammisaduqa")_ (1600 BC)

In the Old [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia") period, the planet Venus was known as Ninsi'anna, and later as Dilbat.[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-211) The name "Ninsi'anna" translates to "divine lady, illumination of heaven", which refers to Venus as the brightest visible "star". Earlier spellings of the name were written with the [cuneiform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuneiform "Cuneiform") sign si4 (= SU, meaning "to be red"), and the original meaning may have been "divine lady of the redness of heaven", in reference to the colour of the morning and evening sky.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Heimpel_1982-212)

The Chinese historically referred to the morning Venus as "the Great White" (_Tàibái_ 太白) or "the Opener (Starter) of Brightness" (_Qǐmíng_ 啟明), and the evening Venus as "the Excellent West One" (_Chánggēng_ 長庚).[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Needham_1959-213)

The ancient Greeks initially believed Venus to be two separate stars: [Phosphorus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phosphorus_(morning_star) "Phosphorus (morning star)"), the morning star, and [Hesperus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hesperus "Hesperus"), the evening star. [Pliny the Elder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder "Pliny the Elder") credited the realization that they were a single object to [Pythagoras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pythagoras "Pythagoras") in the sixth century BC,[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Pliny_1991-214) while [Diogenes Laërtius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diogenes_La%C3%ABrtius "Diogenes Laërtius") argued that [Parmenides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parmenides "Parmenides") (early fifth century) was probably responsible for this discovery.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Berkert_1972-215) Though they recognized Venus as a single object, the ancient Romans continued to designate the morning aspect of Venus as [Lucifer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucifer "Lucifer"), literally "Light-Bringer", and the evening aspect as [Vesper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hesperus "Hesperus"),[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dobbin_2002-216) both of which are literal translations of their traditional Greek names.

In the second century, in his astronomical treatise _[Almagest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almagest "Almagest")_, [Ptolemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ptolemy "Ptolemy") theorized that both Mercury and Venus were located between the Sun and the Earth. The 11th-century [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samanid_Empire "Samanid Empire") astronomer [Avicenna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avicenna "Avicenna") claimed to have observed a [transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus "Transit of Venus") (although there is some doubt about it),[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Goldstein-217) which later astronomers took as confirmation of Ptolemy's theory.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Enc_Irnica-218) In the 12th century, the [Andalusian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") astronomer [Ibn Bajjah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Bajjah "Ibn Bajjah") observed "two planets as black spots on the face of the Sun"; these were thought to be the transits of Venus and Mercury by 13th-century [Maragha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maragheh_observatory "Maragheh observatory") astronomer [Qotb al-Din Shirazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qotb_al-Din_Shirazi "Qotb al-Din Shirazi"), though this cannot be true as there were no Venus transits in Ibn Bajjah's lifetime.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Ansari_2002-219)[[note 3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-222)

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Dresden_Codex_p09.jpg/250px-Dresden_Codex_p09.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dresden_Codex_p09.jpg)

The [Pre-Columbian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era "Pre-Columbian era") Mayan _[Dresden Codex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dresden\_Codex "Dresden Codex")_, which calculates appearances of Venus

### Venus and early modern astronomy

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c2/Phases-of-Venus2.svg/250px-Phases-of-Venus2.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phases-of-Venus2.svg)

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Phases-of-Venus-Geocentric.svg/250px-Phases-of-Venus-Geocentric.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phases-of-Venus-Geocentric.svg)

When the planet was first observed with a telescope in December 1610, by the Italian physicist [Galileo Galilei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei"), he found it showed [phases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_phase "Planetary phase") like the Moon, varying from crescent to gibbous to full and vice versa. When Venus is furthest from the Sun in the sky, it shows a [half-lit phase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elongation_(astronomy) "Elongation (astronomy)"), and when it is closest to the Sun in the sky, it shows as a crescent or full phase. This could be possible only if Venus orbited the Sun, reported by Galileo in his 1613 [Letters on Sunspots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letters_on_Sunspots "Letters on Sunspots"), becoming one of the first observations to clearly contradict the Ptolemaic [geocentric model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geocentric_model "Geocentric model") that the Solar System was concentric and centred on Earth.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-palmieri-223)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Fegley-224)

The 1631 [transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transit_of_Venus "Transit of Venus"), while not recorded, was the first one successfully predicted, by [Johannes Kepler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler") and his calculations, which he published in 1629. The following [1639 transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1639_transit_of_Venus "1639 transit of Venus") was accurately predicted by [Jeremiah Horrocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks "Jeremiah Horrocks") and observed by him and his friend, [William Crabtree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Crabtree "William Crabtree"), at each of their respective homes, on 4 December 1639 (24 November under the [Julian calendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julian_calendar "Julian calendar") in use at that time).[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kollerstrom-225)

[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Lavender_-_Jeremiah_Horrocks_%281618%E2%80%931641%29.jpg/250px-Lavender_-_Jeremiah_Horrocks_%281618%E2%80%931641%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lavender_-_Jeremiah_Horrocks_(1618%E2%80%931641).jpg)

Twentieth century painting of [Jeremiah Horrocks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeremiah_Horrocks "Jeremiah Horrocks") observing the [1639 transit of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1639_transit_of_Venus "1639 transit of Venus").

The [atmosphere of Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus "Atmosphere of Venus") was discovered in 1761 by Russian polymath [Mikhail Lomonosov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov "Mikhail Lomonosov").[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Marov2004-226)[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Britannica-227) Venus's atmosphere was observed in 1790 by German astronomer [Johann Schröter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Schr%C3%B6ter "Johann Schröter"). Schröter found when the planet was a thin crescent, the cusps extended through more than 180°. He correctly surmised this was due to [scattering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scattering "Scattering") of sunlight in a dense atmosphere. Later, American astronomer [Chester Smith Lyman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chester_Smith_Lyman "Chester Smith Lyman") observed a complete ring around the dark side of the planet when it was at [inferior conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inferior_conjunction "Inferior conjunction"), providing further evidence for an atmosphere.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Russell_1899-228) The atmosphere complicated efforts to determine a rotation period for the planet, and observers such as Italian-born astronomer [Giovanni Cassini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Cassini "Giovanni Cassini") and Schröter incorrectly estimated periods of about 24 h from the motions of markings on the planet's apparent surface.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hussey_1832-229)

[![Image 27: A hand-drawn sequence of images showing Venus passing over the edge of the Sun's disk, leaving an illusory drop of shadow behind](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Venus_Drawing.jpg/250px-Venus_Drawing.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_Drawing.jpg)

The "[black drop effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_drop_effect "Black drop effect")" as recorded during the 1769 transit

### Early 20th century advances

Little more was discovered about Venus until the 20th century. Its almost featureless disc gave no hint what its surface might be like, and it was only with the development of [spectroscopic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_spectroscopy "Astronomical spectroscopy") and [ultraviolet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet") observations that more of its secrets were revealed.

The first ultraviolet observations were carried out in the 1920s, when [Frank E. Ross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_E._Ross "Frank E. Ross") found that [ultraviolet photographs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet_photography "Ultraviolet photography") revealed considerable detail that was absent in visible and [infrared](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrared "Infrared") radiation. He suggested this was due to a dense, yellow lower atmosphere with high [cirrus clouds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cirrus_cloud "Cirrus cloud") above it.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Ross_1928-230)

It had been noted that Venus had no discernible [oblateness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oblate_spheroid "Oblate spheroid") in its disk, suggesting a slow rotation, and some astronomers concluded based on this that it was [tidally locked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tidally_locked "Tidally locked") like Mercury was believed to be at the time; but other researchers had detected a significant quantity of heat coming from the planet's nightside, suggesting a quick rotation (a high surface temperature was not suspected at the time), confusing the issue.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Martz_1934-231) Later work in the 1950s showed the rotation was retrograde.

### Space age

The first [interplanetary spaceflight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_spaceflight "Interplanetary spaceflight") attempt was in 1961 when the [robotic space probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncrewed_spacecraft "Uncrewed spacecraft")_[Venera 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_1 "Venera 1")_ of the Soviet [Venera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera "Venera") programme flew to Venus. It lost contact en route.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-mitchell_1-232)

The first successful interplanetary mission, also to Venus, was _[Mariner 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner\_2 "Mariner 2")_ of the United States' [Mariner programme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner_program "Mariner program"), passing on 14 December 1962 at 34,833 km (21,644 mi) above the surface of Venus and gathering data on the planet's atmosphere.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Mayer_et_al_1958-233)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NASA_1962-234)

Additionally [radar observations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radar_astronomy "Radar astronomy") of Venus were first carried out in the 1960s, and provided the first measurements of the rotation period, which were close to the actual value.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Goldstein_Carpenter_1963-235)

_[Venera 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_3 "Venera 3")_, launched in 1966, became humanity's first probe and lander to reach and impact another celestial body other than the Moon, but could not return data as it crashed into the surface of Venus. In 1967, _[Venera 4](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_4 "Venera 4")_ was launched and successfully deployed science experiments in the Venusian atmosphere before impacting. _Venera 4_ showed the surface temperature was hotter than _Mariner 2_ had calculated, at almost 500°C (932°F), determined that the atmosphere was 95% carbon dioxide (CO

2), and discovered that Venus's atmosphere was considerably denser than _Venera 4_'s designers had anticipated.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-mitchell_2-236)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Harvey115-237)

In an early example of space cooperation the data of _Venera 4_ was joined with the 1967 _[Mariner 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner\_5 "Mariner 5")_ data, analysed by a combined Soviet–American science team in a series of colloquia over the following year.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-COSPAR_Group_VII_1969-238)

On 15 December 1970, _[Venera 7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_7 "Venera 7")_ became the first spacecraft to [soft land on another planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landings_on_other_planets "Landings on other planets") and the first to transmit data from there back to Earth.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Time_1971-239)

In 1974, _[Mariner 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariner\_10 "Mariner 10")_ swung by Venus to bend its path towards Mercury and took ultraviolet photographs of the clouds, revealing the extraordinarily high wind speeds in the Venusian atmosphere. This was the first interplanetary [gravity assist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist") ever used, a technique which would be used by later probes.

Radar observations in the 1970s revealed details of the Venusian surface for the first time. Pulses of radio waves were beamed at the planet using the 300 m (1,000 ft) radio telescope at [Arecibo Observatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory "Arecibo Observatory"), and the echoes revealed two highly reflective regions, designated the [Alpha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpha_Regio "Alpha Regio") and [Beta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beta_Regio "Beta Regio") regions. The observations revealed a bright region attributed to mountains, which was called [Maxwell Montes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxwell_Montes "Maxwell Montes").[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Campbell_et_al_1976-240) These three features are now the only ones on Venus that do not have female names.[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-jpl-magellan-50)

[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Foto_de_Venera_9.png/500px-Foto_de_Venera_9.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foto_de_Venera_9.png)

First view and first clear 180-degree panorama of Venus's surface as well as any other planet than Earth (1975, Soviet _[Venera 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_9 "Venera 9")_ lander). Black-and-white image of barren, black, slate-like rocks against a flat sky. The ground and the probe are the focus.

In 1975, the Soviet _[Venera 9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_9 "Venera 9")_ and _[10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_10 "Venera 10")_ landers transmitted the first images from the surface of Venus, which were in black and white. NASA obtained additional data with the [Pioneer Venus project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_Venus_project "Pioneer Venus project"), consisting of two separate missions:[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Colin_Hall_1977-241) the [Pioneer Venus Multiprobe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_Venus_Multiprobe "Pioneer Venus Multiprobe") and [Pioneer Venus Orbiter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_Venus_Orbiter "Pioneer Venus Orbiter"), orbiting Venus between 1978 and 1992.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Williams_2005-242) In 1982 the first monochrome colour filters images of the surface were obtained with the Soviet _[Venera 13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_13 "Venera 13")_ and _[14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_14 "Venera 14")_ landers. After _[Venera 15](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_15 "Venera 15")_ and _[16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venera\_16 "Venera 16")_ operated between 1983 and 1984 in orbit, conducting detailed mapping of 25% of Venus's terrain (from the north pole to 30°N latitude), the Soviet Venera programme came to a close.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Greeley_Batson_2007-243)

[![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Russian_%22Vega%22_balloon_mission_to_Venus_on_display_at_the_Udvar-Hazy_museum.jpg/250px-Russian_%22Vega%22_balloon_mission_to_Venus_on_display_at_the_Udvar-Hazy_museum.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Russian_%22Vega%22_balloon_mission_to_Venus_on_display_at_the_Udvar-Hazy_museum.jpg)

[Vega balloon probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vega_programme "Vega programme") on display at the [Udvar-Hazy Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-Hazy_Center "Steven F. Udvar-Hazy Center") of the [Smithsonian Institution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution "Smithsonian Institution")

In 1985 the Soviet [Vega programme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vega_programme "Vega programme") with its _[Vega 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vega\_1 "Vega 1")_ and _[Vega 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vega\_2 "Vega 2")_ missions carried the last entry probes and carried the first ever extraterrestrial [aerobots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerobot "Aerobot") for the first time achieving atmospheric flight outside Earth by employing inflatable balloons.

Between 1990 and 1994, _[Magellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magellan\_(spacecraft) "Magellan (spacecraft)")_ operated in orbit until deorbiting, mapping the surface of Venus. Furthermore, probes like _[Galileo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo\_(spacecraft) "Galileo (spacecraft)")_ (1990),[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-PDS_Atmospheres_Node_1989-244)_[Cassini–Huygens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens "Cassini–Huygens")_ (1998/1999), and _[MESSENGER](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MESSENGER "MESSENGER")_ (2006/2007) visited Venus with flybys en route to other destinations. In April 2006, _[Venus Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus\_Express "Venus Express")_, the first dedicated Venus mission by the [European Space Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Space_Agency "European Space Agency") (ESA), entered orbit around Venus. _Venus Express_ provided unprecedented observation of Venus's atmosphere. ESA concluded the _Venus Express_ mission in December 2014 deorbiting it in January 2015.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Howell_2014-245)

In 2010, the first successful interplanetary [solar sail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_sail "Solar sail") spacecraft [IKAROS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IKAROS "IKAROS") travelled to Venus for a flyby.

Between 2015 and 2024 Japan's _[Akatsuki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akatsuki\_(spacecraft) "Akatsuki (spacecraft)")_ probe was active in orbit around Venus and [BepiColombo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BepiColombo "BepiColombo") performed flybys in 2020/2021.

[![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Wispr_4thflyby.gif/250px-Wispr_4thflyby.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wispr_4thflyby.gif)

[WISPR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WISPR "WISPR") of the [Parker Solar Probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parker_Solar_Probe "Parker Solar Probe") took this visible light footage of the nightside in 2021, showing the hot faintly glowing surface, and its [Aphrodite Terra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphrodite_Terra "Aphrodite Terra") as large dark patch, through the clouds, which prohibit such observations on the dayside when they are illuminated.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-246)[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Geophysical_Research_Letters_2022-247)

### Active and planned missions

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/VenusLanderTopo.jpg/500px-VenusLanderTopo.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:VenusLanderTopo.jpg)

Global topographic map of Venus, with all probe landing sites marked

As of 2025 there are no active probes at Venus, with [Parker Solar Probe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parker_Solar_Probe "Parker Solar Probe") scheduled to return repeatedly to Venus until 2030.

Several [probes are under development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_missions_to_Venus "List of missions to Venus") as well as multiple proposed missions still in their early conceptual stages. The next Venus mission scheduled is the [Venus Life Finder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_Life_Finder "Venus Life Finder"), expected to launch not earlier than summer 2026.

Indian ISRO is working on [Venus Orbiter Mission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_Orbiter_Mission "Venus Orbiter Mission"), aiming to launch it in 2028. UAE mission to asteroids, [MBR Explorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MBR_Explorer "MBR Explorer"), will perform a flyby of the planet. NASA approved two missions to the planet, [VERITAS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VERITAS_(spacecraft) "VERITAS (spacecraft)") and [DAVINCI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DAVINCI "DAVINCI"), planned to be launched not earlier then 2031. ESA plans to launch [EnVision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EnVision "EnVision") also in 2031.

#### Objectives

Venus has been identified for future research as an important case for understanding:

*   the origins of the solar system and Earth, and if systems and planets like ours are common or rare in the universe.
*   how planetary bodies evolve from their primordial states to today's diverse objects.
*   the development of conditions leading to habitable environments and life.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-O'Rourke_Wilson_Borrelli_Byrne_2023_p.-248)

### Crewed mission concepts

Venus has been considered since the 1960s as a waypoint for [crewed missions to Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crewed_missions_to_Mars "Crewed missions to Mars") through [opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_(astronomy) "Opposition (astronomy)") missions instead of direct [conjunction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conjunction_(astronomy) "Conjunction (astronomy)") missions with Venus [gravity assist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gravity_assist "Gravity assist")[flybys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flyby_(spaceflight) "Flyby (spaceflight)"), demonstrating that they should be quicker and safer missions to [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars"), with better return or abort flight windows, and less or the same amount of radiation exposure from the flight as direct Mars flights.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Rao_2020-249)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Izenberg_McNutt_Runyon_Byrne_2021_pp._100%E2%80%93104-250)

#### Possible atmospheric habitation

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/NASA_Cloud_City_on_Venus.jpg/330px-NASA_Cloud_City_on_Venus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NASA_Cloud_City_on_Venus.jpg)

Artist's rendering of a NASA [High Altitude Venus Operational Concept (HAVOC)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HAVOC "HAVOC") crewed floating outpost on Venus

While the surface conditions of Venus are extremely hostile, the atmospheric pressure, temperature, and solar and cosmic radiation 50 km above the surface are similar to those at Earth's surface ("clement conditions").[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-f997-251)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Herbst_Banjac_Atri_Nordheim_2019_p=A15-116)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Patel_Mason_Nordheim_Dartnell_2022_p=114796-115)[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Taylor_2020-186) Among the many engineering challenges for any human presence in the atmosphere of Venus are the corrosive amounts of [sulfuric acid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulfuric_acid "Sulfuric acid") in the atmosphere.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Landis2003-252)[Aerostats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerostat "Aerostat") for crewed exploration and possibly for permanent "[floating cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Floating_cities_and_islands_in_fiction#Venus "Floating cities and islands in fiction")" in the Venusian atmosphere have been proposed as an alternative to the popular idea of living on [planetary surfaces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_surface "Planetary surface") such as [Mars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars "Mars").[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Landis2003-252)[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-%D0%90%D1%80%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%B2_%D1%84%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8-253)[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Inner_Solar_System_2015-254)[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Tickle_2015-255)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Warmflash_2017-256) NASA's [High Altitude Venus Operational Concept](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Altitude_Venus_Operational_Concept "High Altitude Venus Operational Concept") was a training concept to study a crewed aerostat design.

Search for life
---------------

Speculation on the possibility of life on Venus's surface decreased significantly after the early 1960s when it became clear that conditions were extreme compared to those on Earth. Venus's extreme temperatures and atmospheric pressure make water-based life, as currently known, unlikely.

Some scientists have speculated that thermoacidophilic [extremophile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extremophile "Extremophile")[microorganisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microorganism "Microorganism") might exist in the cooler, acidic upper layers of the Venusian [atmosphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus "Atmosphere of Venus").[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Clark_2003-257)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Redfern_2004-258)[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dartnell2015-259) Such speculations go back to 1967, when [Carl Sagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Sagan "Carl Sagan") and [Harold J. Morowitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_J._Morowitz "Harold J. Morowitz") suggested in a _[Nature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nature\_(journal) "Nature (journal)")_ article that tiny objects detected in Venus's clouds might be organisms similar to Earth's bacteria (which are of approximately the same size):

While the surface conditions of Venus make the hypothesis of life there implausible, the clouds of Venus are a different story altogether. As was pointed out some years ago, water, [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide") and sunlight—the prerequisites for [photosynthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photosynthesis "Photosynthesis")—are plentiful in the vicinity of the clouds.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Sagan_Morowitz_1967-260)
In August 2019, astronomers led by Yeon Joo Lee reported that long-term pattern of absorbance and [albedo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albedo "Albedo") changes in the atmosphere of the planet Venus caused by "unknown absorbers", which may be chemicals or even large colonies of microorganisms high up in the atmosphere of the planet, affect the climate.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-TAJ-20190826-139) Their [light absorbance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_absorption "Light absorption") is almost identical to that of micro-organisms in Earth's clouds. Similar conclusions have been reached by other studies.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-ES-20190903-261)

In September 2020, a team of astronomers led by [Jane Greaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jane_Greaves "Jane Greaves") from [Cardiff University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardiff_University "Cardiff University") announced the likely detection of [phosphine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phosphine "Phosphine"), a gas not known to be produced by any known chemical processes on the Venusian surface or atmosphere, in the upper levels of the planet's clouds.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Bains_et_al_2021-262)[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Greaves_et_al_2020-118)[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Drake_2020-117)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Perkins_2020-263)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Seager_et_al_2020-264) One proposed source for this phosphine is living organisms.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Sample1-265) The phosphine was detected at heights of at least 30 miles (48 km) above the surface, and primarily at mid-latitudes with none detected at the poles. The discovery prompted [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA") administrator [Jim Bridenstine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Bridenstine "Jim Bridenstine") to publicly call for a new focus on the study of Venus, describing the phosphine find as "the most significant development yet in building the case for life off Earth".[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kooser_2020-266)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Bridenstine_2020-267)

Subsequent analysis of the data-processing used to identify phosphine in the atmosphere of Venus has raised concerns that the detection-line may be an artefact. The use of a 12th-order polynomial fit may have amplified noise and generated a false reading (see [Runge's phenomenon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Runge%27s_phenomenon "Runge's phenomenon")). Observations of the atmosphere of Venus at other parts of the electromagnetic spectrum in which a phosphine absorption line would be expected did not detect phosphine.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Plait1-268) By late October 2020, re-analysis of data with a proper subtraction of background did not show a [statistically significant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistically_significant "Statistically significant") detection of phosphine.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Snellen_et_al_2020-269)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Thompson2020-270)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cordiner_et_al_2021-271)

Members of the team around Greaves, are working as part of a project by the [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT "MIT") to send with the rocket company [Rocket Lab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocket_Lab "Rocket Lab") the first private interplanetary space craft, to look for organics by entering the atmosphere of Venus with a probe named [Venus Life Finder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_Life_Finder "Venus Life Finder").[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Venus_Cloud_Life_-_MIT_2023-272)

### Planetary protection

The [Committee on Space Research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_on_Space_Research "Committee on Space Research") is a scientific organization established by the [International Council for Science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Council_for_Science "International Council for Science"). Among their responsibilities is the development of recommendations for avoiding [interplanetary contamination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interplanetary_contamination "Interplanetary contamination"). For this purpose, space missions are categorized into five groups. Due to the harsh surface environment of Venus, Venus has been under the [planetary protection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_protection "Planetary protection") category two.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-NRC_2006-273) This indicates that there is only a remote chance that spacecraft-borne contamination could compromise investigations.

In culture
----------

Venus is among the most prominent features in the night sky, and has been treated as particularly important in [mythology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_(mythology) "Venus (mythology)"), [astrology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planets_in_astrology#Venus "Planets in astrology") and [fiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_in_fiction "Venus in fiction") across many different cultures.

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Kudurru_Melishipak_Louvre_Sb23_n02.jpg/330px-Kudurru_Melishipak_Louvre_Sb23_n02.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kudurru_Melishipak_Louvre_Sb23_n02.jpg)

The [eight-pointed star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octagram "Octagram") is a symbol used in some cultures to represent Venus, sometimes combined into a [star and crescent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_and_crescent "Star and crescent") arrangement. Here, the eight pointed star is the [Star of Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_of_Ishtar "Star of Ishtar"), the [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia") Venus goddess, alongside the [solar disk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_symbol "Solar symbol") of her brother [Shamash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shamash "Shamash") and the [crescent moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crescent "Crescent") of their father [Sin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sin_(mythology) "Sin (mythology)") on a [boundary stone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kudurru "Kudurru") of [Meli-Shipak II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meli-Shipak_II "Meli-Shipak II"), dating to the 12th century BC.

Several hymns praise [Inanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna "Inanna") in her role as the goddess of the planet Venus.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Green1992-274)[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nemet-Nejat-275) Theology professor Jeffrey Cooley has argued that, in many myths, Inanna's movements may correspond with the movements of the planet Venus in the sky.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) The discontinuous movements of Venus relate to both mythology as well as Inanna's dual nature.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) In _Inanna's Descent to the Underworld_, unlike any other deity, Inanna is able to descend into the netherworld and return to the heavens. The planet Venus appears to make a similar descent, setting in the West and then rising again in the East.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) An introductory hymn describes Inanna leaving the heavens and heading for _Kur_, what could be presumed to be, the mountains, replicating the rising and setting of Inanna to the West.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) In _[Inanna and Shukaletuda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna\_and\_Shukaletuda "Inanna and Shukaletuda")_ and _[Inanna's Descent into the Underworld](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna%27s\_Descent\_into\_the\_Underworld "Inanna's Descent into the Underworld")_ appear to parallel the motion of the planet Venus.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208) In _Inanna and Shukaletuda_, Shukaletuda is described as scanning the heavens in search of Inanna, possibly searching the eastern and western horizons.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley2-276) In the same myth, while searching for her attacker, Inanna herself makes several movements that correspond with the movements of Venus in the sky.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cooley-208)

Via [Mesopotamian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia") influence, it is possible that the [Ancient Egyptians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt "Ancient Egypt") and [Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greeks "Ancient Greeks") knew that the morning star and the evening star were one and the same as early as the second millennium BC—or the [Late Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Period_of_ancient_Egypt "Late Period of ancient Egypt") at the latest.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Parker_1974-277)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Quack_2019-278) The Egyptians knew the morning star as _Tioumoutiri_ and the evening star as _Ouaiti_.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cattermole_Moore_1997-279) They depicted Venus at first as a [phoenix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_(mythology) "Phoenix (mythology)") or [heron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heron "Heron") (see [Bennu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bennu "Bennu")),[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Parker_1974-277) calling it 'the crosser' or 'star with crosses',[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Parker_1974-277) associating it with [Osiris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osiris "Osiris"), and later depicting it as two-headed (with human or falcon heads), and associated it with [Horus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horus "Horus"),[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Quack_2019-278) son of [Isis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isis "Isis") (which during the even later [Hellenistic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period "Hellenistic period") was together with [Hathor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hathor "Hathor") identified with [Aphrodite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphrodite "Aphrodite")). The Greeks used the names _[Phōsphoros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ph%C5%8Dsphoros "Phōsphoros")_, meaning 'light-bringer' (whence the element [phosphorus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phosphorus "Phosphorus"); alternately _Ēōsphoros_, meaning 'dawn-bringer'), for the morning star, and _[Hesperos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hesperos "Hesperos")_, meaning 'Western one', for the evening star,[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-EBLCM-280) both children of dawn [Eos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eos "Eos") and therefore grandchildren of Aphrodite. Though by the Roman era they were recognized as one celestial object, known as "the star of [Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_(mythology) "Venus (mythology)")", the traditional two Greek names continued to be used, though usually translated to Latin as _[Lucifer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucifer "Lucifer")_ and _[Vesper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hesperus "Hesperus")_.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-EBLCM-280)[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Cicero-281)

Classical poets such as [Homer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homer "Homer"), [Sappho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sappho "Sappho"), [Ovid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ovid "Ovid") and [Virgil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgil "Virgil") spoke of the star and its light.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Atsma-282) Poets such as [William Blake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Blake "William Blake"), [Robert Frost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Frost "Robert Frost"), [Letitia Elizabeth Landon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Letitia_Elizabeth_Landon "Letitia Elizabeth Landon"), [Alfred Lord Tennyson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_Lord_Tennyson "Alfred Lord Tennyson") and [William Wordsworth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Wordsworth "William Wordsworth") wrote odes to it.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Sobel_2005-283) The composer [Holst](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gustav_Holst "Gustav Holst") included it as [the second movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Planets#Venus "The Planets") of his _[The Planets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Planets "The Planets")_ suite.

In India, the name for Venus in Sanskrit was _Shukra Graha_, meaning 'the planet Shukra'—in reference to [Shukra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shukra "Shukra"), a powerful saint. As appears in [Vedic astrology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedic_astrology "Vedic astrology"),[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-bhalla06-284) the Sanskrit name _Shukra_ means 'clear, pure' or 'brightness, clearness'. One of the nine [Navagraha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navagraha "Navagraha"), it is held to affect wealth, pleasure and reproduction; it was the son of [Bhrgu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhrgu "Bhrgu"), preceptor of the Daityas, and guru of the Asuras.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-behari_frawley03-285)

The English name _Venus_ stems originally from the [ancient Romans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_religion "Roman religion"). Romans named Venus after [their goddess of love](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_(goddess) "Venus (goddess)"), who in turn was based on the [ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek_religion "Ancient Greek religion") love goddess [Aphrodite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aphrodite "Aphrodite"),[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Getty-286) who was herself based on the similar [Sumerian religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumerian_religion "Sumerian religion") goddess [Inanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna "Inanna") (which is Ishtar in [Akkadian religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkadian_religion "Akkadian religion")), all of whom were associated with the planet.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Nemet-Nejat-275)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Green1992-274) The [weekday of the planet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_hours "Planetary hours") and these goddesses is [Friday](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friday "Friday"), named after the Germanic goddess [Frigg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frigg "Frigg"), who has been associated with the Roman goddess Venus.

In Chinese, the planet is called _Jinxing_ (金星; 'metal star'); of the [five elements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Five_elements_(Chinese_philosophy) "Five elements (Chinese philosophy)") of traditional Chinese philosophy, Venus was historically associated with [metal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metal_(wuxing) "Metal (wuxing)"). These traditions are shared among modern [Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_culture "Chinese culture"), [Japanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_culture "Japanese culture"), [Korean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_culture "Korean culture") and [Vietnamese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_Vietnam "Culture of Vietnam") cultures, including a name for the planet literally meaning 'metal star' (金星) in each language.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-De_Groot_1912-287)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Crump_1992-288)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Hulbert_1909-289)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-VOER-290)

The [Maya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya_civilisation "Maya civilisation") considered Venus to be the most important celestial body after the Sun and Moon. They called it _Chac ek_,[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Volume_7_of_Mayan_studies-291) or _Noh Ek'_, 'the Great Star'.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Milbrath-292) The cycles of Venus were important to their calendar and were described in some of their books, such as the _[Maya Codex of Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya\_Codex\_of\_Mexico "Maya Codex of Mexico")_ and _[Dresden Codex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dresden\_Codex "Dresden Codex")_. The [flag of Chile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_Chile "Flag of Chile") (_Estrella Solitaria_, 'Lone Star') depicts Venus.

### Modern culture

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/250px-Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Van_Gogh_-_Starry_Night_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg)

Venus is portrayed just to the right of the large cypress tree in [Vincent van Gogh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh "Vincent van Gogh")'s 1889 painting _[The Starry Night](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Starry\_Night "The Starry Night")_.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Whitney_1986-293)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Boime_1984-294)

The impenetrable Venusian cloud cover gave science fiction writers free rein to speculate on conditions at its surface; all the more so when early observations showed that not only was it similar in size to Earth, it possessed a substantial atmosphere. Closer to the Sun than Earth, the planet was often depicted as warmer, but still [habitable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability") by humans.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-miller-295) The genre reached its peak between the 1930s and 1950s, at a time when science had revealed some aspects of Venus, but not yet the harsh reality of its surface conditions. Findings from the first missions to Venus showed reality to be quite different and brought this particular genre to an end.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Dick_2001-296) As scientific knowledge of Venus advanced, science fiction authors tried to keep pace, particularly by conjecturing human attempts to [terraform Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terraforming_of_Venus "Terraforming of Venus").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Seed_2005-297)

### Symbols

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Venus_symbol_%28planetary_color%29.svg/80px-Venus_symbol_%28planetary_color%29.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Venus_symbol_(planetary_color).svg)

The symbol of a circle with a small cross beneath is the so-called [Venus symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus_symbol "Venus symbol"), gaining its name for being used as the [astronomical symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomical_symbol "Astronomical symbol") for Venus. The symbol is of [ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek "Ancient Greek") origin, and represents more generally [femininity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Femininity "Femininity"), adopted by biology as [gender symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_symbol "Gender symbol") for female,[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Schott_2005_pp._1509%E2%80%931510-298)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn1961-299)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn-300) like the [Mars symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_symbol "Mars symbol") for male and sometimes the [Mercury symbol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_symbol "Mercury symbol") for [hermaphrodite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermaphrodite "Hermaphrodite"). This gendered association of Venus and Mars has been used to pair them [heteronormatively](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heteronormative "Heteronormative"), describing women and men stereotypically as being so different that they can be understood as coming from different planets, an understanding popularized in 1992 by the book titled _[Men Are from Mars, Women Are from Venus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men\_Are\_from\_Mars,\_Women\_Are\_from\_Venus "Men Are from Mars, Women Are from Venus")_.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Brammer_2020-301)

The Venus symbol was also used in Western [alchemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alchemy "Alchemy") representing the element [copper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copper "Copper") (like the symbol of [Mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercury_(planet) "Mercury (planet)") is also the symbol of the [element mercury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Element_mercury "Element mercury")),[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn1961-299)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn-300) and since polished copper has been used for mirrors from antiquity the symbol for Venus has sometimes been called Venus mirror, representing the mirror of the goddess, although this origin has been discredited as an unlikely origin.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn1961-299)[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-stearn-300)

Besides the Venus symbol, many other symbols have been associated with Venus, other common ones are the [crescent or particularly the star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_and_crescent "Star and crescent"), as with the [Star of Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_of_Ishtar "Star of Ishtar").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-302)

Notes
-----

1.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_ref-67)**Misstated as "Ganiki Chasma" in the press release and scientific publication.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Lakdawalla2015-66)
2.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_ref-176)**It is important to be clear about the meaning of "closeness". In the astronomical literature, the term "closest planets" often refers to the two planets that approach each other the most closely. In other words, the orbits of the two planets approach each other most closely. However, this does not mean that the two planets are closest over time. Essentially because Mercury is closer to the Sun than Venus, Mercury spends more time in proximity to Earth; it could, therefore, be said that Mercury is the planet that is "closest to Earth when averaged over time". However, using this time-average definition of "closeness", it turns out that Mercury is the closest planet to _all_ other planets in the solar system. For that reason, arguably, the proximity-definition is not particularly helpful. An episode of the BBC Radio 4 programme "More or Less" explains the different notions of proximity well.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-MoreOrLess-175)
3.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_ref-222)**Several claims of transit observations made by mediaeval Islamic astronomers have been shown to be sunspots.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-VaqueroV%C3%A1zquez2009-220) Avicenna did not record the date of his observation. There was a transit of Venus within his lifetime, on 24 May 1032, although it is questionable whether it would have been visible from his location.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_note-Kennard-221)

56.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Venus#cite_ref-57)**Hahn, Rebecca M.; Byrne, Paul K. (April 2023). "A Morphological and Spatial Analysis of Volcanoes on Venus". _Journal of Geophysical Research: Planets_. **128** (4): e2023JE007753. [Bibcode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier) "Bibcode (identifier)"):[2023JGRE..12807753H](https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2023JGRE..12807753H). [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1029/2023JE007753](https://doi.org/10.1029%2F2023JE007753). [S2CID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2CID_(identifier) "S2CID (identifier)")[257745255](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:257745255). With the Magellan synthetic-aperture radar full-resolution radar map left- and right-look global mosaics at 75 m-per-pixel resolution, we developed a global catalogue of volcanoes on Venus that contains ~85,000 edifices, ~99% of which are <5 km in diameter. We find that Venus hosts far more volcanoes than previously mapped, and that although they are distributed across virtually the entire planet, size–frequency distribution analysis reveals a relative lack of edifices in the 20–100 km diameter range, which could be related to magma availability and eruption rate.
